1. Clinical question

Clinical English: Summarize the clinically relevant warnings, contraindications, and high-priority use restrictions for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: What are the key warnings and contraindications?

Question family: warnings_contra

Answer

Across the retrieved PMDA sources for chlorhexidine gluconate, the most consistent high-priority restrictions involve the following points: (e-IF) became the principle. In line with this change, if there is a revision to the package insert such as ``addition of indications'' or ``revised warnings, contraindications, and important basic precautions'', the latest version of Stericlone® R liquid with added rationale for the revision. Additional clinically relevant restriction(s) include "In order to predict reactions such as shock and anaphylaxis, be sure to thoroughly inquire about your history of hypersensitivity to chlorhexidine preparations and whether you have a predisposition to drug sensitivity before use.". Further caution is supported by (1) Concomitant use contraindications and reasons not applicable (2) Precautions for concomitant use and reasons not applicable. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • (e-IF) became the principle. In line with this change, if there is a revision to the package insert such as ``addition of indications'' or ``revised warnings, contraindications, and important basic precautions'', the latest version of Stericlone® R liquid with added rationale for the revision.
  • "In order to predict reactions such as shock and anaphylaxis, be sure to thoroughly inquire about your history of hypersensitivity to chlorhexidine preparations and whether you have a predisposition to drug sensitivity before use."
  • (1) Concomitant use contraindications and reasons not applicable (2) Precautions for concomitant use and reasons not applicable
  • [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows.
  • Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.
  • (Explanation) *1 Chlorhexidine at a concentration of 0.5% or higher is highly toxic to the eyes, and if high concentrations of chlorhexidine enter the eye, serious corneal damage will occur15). *2 When diluted with purified water or tap water, chlorhexidine gluconate, which has mild potency, may be contaminated with bacteria such as Pseudomonas spp. and Serratia marcescens. Therefore, it should be sterilized after preparation16).

2. Clinical question

Clinical English: List the clinically relevant contraindications reported for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: What are the contraindications?

Question family: contraindication

Answer

The retrieved PMDA evidence for chlorhexidine gluconate indicates the following key points: (e-IF) became the principle. In line with this change, if there is a revision to the package insert such as ``addition of indications'' or ``revised warnings, contraindications, and important basic precautions'', the latest version of Stericlone® R liquid with added rationale for the revision. Additional relevant detail includes (1) Administration route: Do not use for any purpose other than hand disinfection. (2) When using: Be careful as there are reports that chemical skin burns may occur if the solution is in contact with the skin for a long period of time.. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • (e-IF) became the principle. In line with this change, if there is a revision to the package insert such as ``addition of indications'' or ``revised warnings, contraindications, and important basic precautions'', the latest version of Stericlone® R liquid with added rationale for the revision.
  • (1) Administration route: Do not use for any purpose other than hand disinfection. (2) When using: Be careful as there are reports that chemical skin burns may occur if the solution is in contact with the skin for a long period of time.
  • (1) Concomitant use contraindications and reasons not applicable (2) Precautions for concomitant use and reasons not applicable
  • (1) Administration route Do not use for any purpose other than hand disinfection. (2) During use
  • エタノール溶液(2分以上)手術室・病室・家具・器具・物品などの消毒
  • (本剤の100倍希釈) 0.05%水溶液

Original question: What are the approved indications and dosage instructions?

Question family: general

Answer

The retrieved PMDA evidence for chlorhexidine gluconate indicates the following key points: (3) Origin of name: The dosage form and content of the active ingredient, chlorhexidine gluconate, are listed, and "NP" is added from NIPRO. Additional relevant detail includes Standards and contents without regulatory classification for liquid dosage forms. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • (3) Origin of name: The dosage form and content of the active ingredient, chlorhexidine gluconate, are listed, and "NP" is added from NIPRO.
  • Standards and contents without regulatory classification for liquid dosage forms
  • Dosage form liquid drug specifications/content
  • Created in September 2024 (1st edition)
  • Pharmaceutical interview form
  • Created in accordance with the Japan Society of Hospital Pharmacists' IF writing guidelines 2018 (updated in 2019)

4. Clinical question

Clinical English: What are the important precautions before using this drug for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: What are the important precautions before using this drug?

Question family: warning

Answer

The retrieved PMDA evidence for chlorhexidine gluconate indicates the following key points: [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows. Additional relevant detail includes Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows.
  • Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.
  • Shock and anaphylaxis may occur, so carefully monitor the product. If decreased blood pressure, hives, difficulty breathing, etc. occur, immediately discontinue use and take appropriate measures. ”
  • (Explanation) *1 Chlorhexidine at a concentration of 0.5% or higher is highly toxic to the eyes, and if high concentrations of chlorhexidine enter the eye, serious corneal damage will occur15). *2 When diluted with purified water or tap water, chlorhexidine gluconate, which has mild potency, may be contaminated with bacteria such as Pseudomonas spp. and Serratia marcescens. Therefore, it should be sterilized after preparation16).
  • Refer to "VIII. Items related to safety (precautions, etc.)", "2. Contraindications and their reasons (including contraindications in principle)", "6. Important basic precautions, their reasons and treatment methods", "8. Side effects", "14. Precautions for application".
  • See "VIII. Items related to safety (precautions, etc.)", "2. Contraindications and their reasons (including contraindications in principle)", "6. Important basic precautions, their reasons and treatment methods", "8. Side effects", "14. Precautions for application".

8. Clinical question

Clinical English: Summarize the major adverse reactions and serious safety findings reported for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: What are the major adverse reactions and serious adverse events?

Question family: adverse

Answer

The retrieved safety material for chlorhexidine gluconate indicates the following adverse-event findings: Ru. (12) Shock and anaphylaxis may occur as serious side effects. Further adverse-reaction information includes (3) Shock and anaphylaxis have been reported as serious side effects (frequency unknown).. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • Ru. (12) Shock and anaphylaxis may occur as serious side effects.
  • (3) Shock and anaphylaxis have been reported as serious side effects (frequency unknown).
  • (1) Effective against Gram-positive and -negative bacteria, fungi, Mycobacterium tuberculosis, and some viruses including HBV (hepatitis B virus) and HIV (human immunodeficiency virus). (2) It dries quickly, and its bactericidal action is rapid and long-lasting. (3) Shock and anaphylaxis have been reported as serious side effects of chlorhexidine gluconate.
  • (1) A preparation containing 1% chlorhexidine gluconate and ethanol, which has an antimicrobial spectrum against various bacteria (excluding bacterial spores) including gram-negative bacteria, gram-positive bacteria, and acid-fast bacteria, and fungi. (2) As a quick-drying hand rub, it exhibits a bactericidal effect immediately after disinfection and a long-lasting effect, making it suitable for hand disinfection during surgery. (3) In consideration of reducing hand roughness, sodium hyaluronate and sodium d1-pyrrolidonecarboxylate liquid are added as moisturizing ingredients. (4) A low-viscosity lotion type designed to prevent spillage when you pick it up. (5) Side effects: Serious side effects (incidence unknown) Shock and anaphylactic symptoms have been reported.
  • (1) This agent shows almost the same antibacterial effect as the Japanese Pharmacopoeia chlorhexidine gluconate solution. (See section VI-2-(2) Test results supporting drug efficacy.) (2) It has a sterilizing effect through foaming and cleaning effects, and is recognized to be fast-acting and long-lasting. (Refer to "VI-2-(2) Test results supporting drug efficacy" and "VI-2-(3) Time of onset and duration of action") (3) It is easy to use as it does not require preparation at the time of use and can be used as is. (Refer to section "V-3-(1) Explanation of usage and administration") (4) Efficacy is not easily inactivated even in the presence of organic substances such as blood and body fluids. (See section "VI-2-(2) Test results supporting drug efficacy") (5) Shock and anaphylaxis have been recognized as serious side effects. (Refer to “VIII-8-(1) Serious side effects and initial symptoms”)
  • serious side effects

34. Clinical question

Answer

The retrieved PMDA formulation sections for chlorhexidine gluconate describe the product composition and dosage-form characteristics as follows: Decomposition of this drug produces p-chloroaniline. Additional composition-related detail includes Pharmaceutical properties Microshield4 (MICROSHIELD4) is a hand disinfectant developed by Johnson & Johnson Medical Pty Ltd. It is a formulation containing chlorhexidine gluconate as an active ingredient. Chlorhexidine gluconate exhibits antibacterial activity against a wide range of Gram-positive and -negative bacteria, and is widely used as a hand disinfectant.. Potentially relevant excipient or formulation information is also noted in Dated June 2, 2004, Pharmaceutical and Shokuhou No. 0602009 “Strengthening measures to prevent pharmaceutical-related medical accidents”.     • I. Items related to overview
    • 1. Development history
    • Povidone-iodine preparations are the mainstream for hand and skin disinfection in medical institutions, but they have drawbacks such as being difficult to dry and taking a long time to develop their effects. In addition, although alcohol preparations have excellent immediate disinfecting effects, they also have the disadvantage of short lasting activity. On the other hand, there are reports that chlorhexidine gluconate has a longer-lasting disinfectant effect than povidone-iodine preparations, and that it suppresses the incidence of surgical site infections and catheter-related bloodstream infections 1), 2). Among these, alcohol-containing chlorhexidine gluconate is said to be the best disinfectant for vascular access skin disinfection because it combines the sustained activity of chlorhexidine gluconate with the immediate action of alcohol2). CDC Guidelines for Preventing Intravascular Catheter-Related Infections from the U.S. Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC)
    • In (2011), disinfection of the puncture site before insertion of central venous catheters and terminal arterial catheters.

35. Clinical question

Clinical English: Identify excipient-related warnings and precautions reported for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: Are there warnings about preservatives, dyes, coating agents, or alcohol-containing excipients?

Question family: formulation

Answer

The retrieved PMDA formulation sections for chlorhexidine gluconate describe the product composition and dosage-form characteristics as follows: Attachment 3 Additional composition-related detail includes 261 Germicidal disinfectant. Potentially relevant excipient or formulation information is also noted in [Drug name] Chlorhexidine gluconate. Evidence was retrieved from 5 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • Attachment 3
  • 261 Germicidal disinfectant
  • [Drug name] Chlorhexidine gluconate
  • [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows.
  • Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.
  • (Explanation) *1 Chlorhexidine at a concentration of 0.5% or higher is highly toxic to the eyes, and if high concentrations of chlorhexidine enter the eye, serious corneal damage will occur15). *2 When diluted with purified water or tap water, chlorhexidine gluconate, which has mild potency, may be contaminated with bacteria such as Pseudomonas spp. and Serratia marcescens. Therefore, it should be sterilized after preparation16).

The retrieved stability-related material for chlorhexidine gluconate mainly addresses storage conditions, shelf-life, and condition-dependent change(s): (1) Appearance/Properties Chlorhexidine gluconate solution is a colorless to slightly yellow, clear liquid with no odor and a bitter taste. 50. Clinical question

Clinical English: What formulation warnings should be reviewed before reformulation for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: What formulation warnings should be reviewed before reformulation?

Question family: formulation

Answer

The retrieved PMDA formulation sections for chlorhexidine gluconate describe the product composition and dosage-form characteristics as follows: Attachment 3 Additional composition-related detail includes 261 Germicidal disinfectant. Potentially relevant excipient or formulation information is also noted in [Drug name] Chlorhexidine gluconate. Evidence was retrieved from 5 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • Attachment 3
  • 261 Germicidal disinfectant
  • [Drug name] Chlorhexidine gluconate
  • [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows.
  • Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.
  • (Explanation) *1 Chlorhexidine at a concentration of 0.5% or higher is highly toxic to the eyes, and if high concentrations of chlorhexidine enter the eye, serious corneal damage will occur15). *2 When diluted with purified water or tap water, chlorhexidine gluconate, which has mild potency, may be contaminated with bacteria such as Pseudomonas spp. and Serratia marcescens. Therefore, it should be sterilized after preparation16).

    • 6. Important basic precautions, their reasons and treatment methods
    • (1) In order to predict reactions such as shock and anaphylaxis, please conduct a thorough interview regarding your history of hypersensitivity to chlorhexidine preparations and whether you have a predisposition to drug hypersensitivity before use. (2) Be sure to dilute this drug and use with caution when using the concentration*1. (3) The diluted aqueous solution of this drug used on the wound site should be sterilized after preparation. (4) Do not use for obstetrics and gynecology (disinfecting the vagina and vulva, etc.) or urology (disinfecting the bladder and external genitalia, etc.)*2.
    • (Explanation) *1 In order to always expect a stable disinfectant effect, it is necessary to prepare and use a disinfectant with an appropriate concentration, taking into account the target pathogen and the shape and material of the target object. In general, it is thought that the higher the concentration of the disinfectant, the more effective the disinfectant will be, but if the concentration is higher than necessary, it may affect the human body (side effects), cause deterioration of the material of the object, and is also an economic problem. On the other hand, if the concentration of the disinfectant is too low, the expected disinfection effect may not be obtained and hospitals may
  • chlorhexidine gluconate | interview_form | page 5 | section=warning | score=6.281539096385685

    • I. Items related to overview
    • 1. Development history
    • Chlorhexidine gluconate is a biguanide disinfectant that has a broad antimicrobial spectrum against Gram-positive and Gram-negative bacteria and exhibits rapid bactericidal action even at low concentrations. Chlorhexidine gluconate preparations are currently commercialized in Japan as 20w/v% liquid preparations, 5w/v% liquid preparations, and sterile preparations that have already been prepared to use concentrations. The concentrated solution is prepared by diluting it into an aqueous solution or an alcoholic solution of various concentrations depending on the purpose, and is sterilized as necessary before use. Furthermore, hand rub disinfectants containing 4w/v% chlorhexidine gluconate/scrubbing agents and ethanol are also widely used for the purpose of hand disinfection. Stericlone® Liquid 5 is a red aqueous solution containing 5w/v% of this chlorhexidine gluconate and added with a nonionic surfactant and a dye (Red No. 2).

    • I. Items related to overview
    • 1. Development history
    • Povidone-iodine preparations are the mainstream for hand and skin disinfection in medical institutions, but they have drawbacks such as being difficult to dry and taking a long time to develop their effects. In addition, although alcohol preparations have excellent immediate disinfecting effects, they also have the disadvantage of short lasting activity. On the other hand, there are reports that chlorhexidine gluconate has a longer-lasting disinfectant effect than povidone-iodine preparations, and that it suppresses the incidence of surgical site infections and catheter-related bloodstream infections 1), 2). Among these, alcohol-containing chlorhexidine gluconate is said to be the best disinfectant for vascular access skin disinfection because it combines the sustained activity of chlorhexidine gluconate with the immediate action of alcohol2). CDC Guidelines for Preventing Intravascular Catheter-Related Infections from the U.S. Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC)
    • In (2011), disinfection of the puncture site before insertion of central venous catheters and terminal arterial catheters.

83. Clinical question

Clinical English: What additional pharmacovigilance activities are described for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: What additional pharmacovigilance activities are described?

Question family: general

Answer

The retrieved PMDA evidence for chlorhexidine gluconate indicates the following key points: Sales began on August 25, 2008. (Accepted based on Pharmaceutical Food and Food Safety No. 0331015 (March 31, 2005)) Additional relevant detail includes has been done. Additionally, the ``Guidelines for Standard Dialysis Operations and Infection Prevention in Dialysis Facilities (Sixth Edition)'' recommends using alcohol containing 1% or more of chlorhexidine gluconate to disinfect the skin at the puncture site, when inserting a dialysis catheter, and at the skin exit after insertion at the start of dialysis. As a result, there is an increasing demand for alcohol-containing preparations with 1% chlorhexidine gluconate as the active ingredient. ``Nipro'' is a formulation in which non-woven fabric is impregnated with a drug solution containing 1% chlorhexidine gluconate in ethanol as an active ingredient.``Nipro'' is a generic drug product with chlorhexidine gluconate in ethanol as a 1% ethanol solution 12 cotton swabs ``LT''. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • Sales began on August 25, 2008. (Accepted based on Pharmaceutical Food and Food Safety No. 0331015 (March 31, 2005))
  • has been done. Additionally, the ``Guidelines for Standard Dialysis Operations and Infection Prevention in Dialysis Facilities (Sixth Edition)'' recommends using alcohol containing 1% or more of chlorhexidine gluconate to disinfect the skin at the puncture site, when inserting a dialysis catheter, and at the skin exit after insertion at the start of dialysis. As a result, there is an increasing demand for alcohol-containing preparations with 1% chlorhexidine gluconate as the active ingredient. ``Nipro'' is a formulation in which non-woven fabric is impregnated with a drug solution containing 1% chlorhexidine gluconate in ethanol as an active ingredient.``Nipro'' is a generic drug product with chlorhexidine gluconate in ethanol as a 1% ethanol solution 12 cotton swabs ``LT''
  • The company planned a commercialization project, received approval in April 2021, and began sales in June of the same year.
  • 2. Therapeutic properties of the product
  • (1) Effective against Gram-positive and -negative bacteria, fungi, Mycobacterium tuberculosis, and some viruses including HBV (hepatitis B virus) and HIV (human immunodeficiency virus). (2) It dries quickly, and its bactericidal action is rapid and long-lasting. (3) Shock and anaphylaxis have been reported as serious side effects of chlorhexidine gluconate.

92. Clinical question

Clinical English: Are there safety warnings about fulminant hepatitis, severe skin reactions, or interstitial pneumonia for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: Are there safety warnings about fulminant hepatitis, severe skin reactions, or interstitial pneumonia?

Question family: warning

Answer

The retrieved PMDA evidence for chlorhexidine gluconate indicates the following key points: [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows. Additional relevant detail includes Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows.
  • Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.
  • Shock and anaphylaxis may occur, so carefully monitor the product. If decreased blood pressure, hives, difficulty breathing, etc. occur, immediately discontinue use and take appropriate measures. ”
  • (Explanation) *1 Chlorhexidine at a concentration of 0.5% or higher is highly toxic to the eyes, and if high concentrations of chlorhexidine enter the eye, serious corneal damage will occur15). *2 When diluted with purified water or tap water, chlorhexidine gluconate, which has mild potency, may be contaminated with bacteria such as Pseudomonas spp. and Serratia marcescens. Therefore, it should be sterilized after preparation16).
  • Refer to "VIII. Items related to safety (precautions, etc.)", "2. Contraindications and their reasons (including contraindications in principle)", "6. Important basic precautions, their reasons and treatment methods", "8. Side effects", "14. Precautions for application".
  • See "VIII. Items related to safety (precautions, etc.)", "2. Contraindications and their reasons (including contraindications in principle)", "6. Important basic precautions, their reasons and treatment methods", "8. Side effects", "14. Precautions for application".

95. Clinical question

Clinical English: Summarize the pregnancy- and lactation-related precautions reported for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: Are there warnings related to pregnancy, fetal risk, or oligohydramnios?

Question family: pregnancy

Answer

The retrieved PMDA evidence for chlorhexidine gluconate indicates the following key points: Chlorhexidine gluconate for 10 days from the 6th to 15th gestation day of pregnant rats. Additional relevant detail includes Slight irritation sensitivity and suppression of weight gain were observed, but no abnormalities were observed in the number of implantations, number of absorbed embryos, number of fetuses, sex ratio, abnormal external appearance, or skeletal variation.. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • Chlorhexidine gluconate for 10 days from the 6th to 15th gestation day of pregnant rats.
  • Slight irritation sensitivity and suppression of weight gain were observed, but no abnormalities were observed in the number of implantations, number of absorbed embryos, number of fetuses, sex ratio, abnormal external appearance, or skeletal variation.
  • Pregnant rats received 10, 25, and 50 mg/kg/day of chlorhexidine gluconate for 10 days from the 6th to 15th gestation day.
  • When administered orally, slight hypersensitivity and suppression of weight gain were observed in the mother at the maximum dose, but no abnormalities were observed in the number of implantations, number of respiratory embryos, number of fetuses, sex ratio, external shape, or skeleton19). (4) Other special toxicities
  • 15.Other notes
  • It has been reported that IgE antibodies specific to chlorhexidine were detected in the serum of several patients who developed shock symptoms due to administration of chlorhexidine gluconate preparations.

97. Clinical question

Clinical English: Are there metabolism-related warnings such as CYP2D6 ultrarapid metabolizer risk for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: Are there metabolism-related warnings such as CYP2D6 ultrarapid metabolizer risk?

Question family: warning

Answer

The retrieved PMDA evidence for chlorhexidine gluconate indicates the following key points: [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows. Additional relevant detail includes Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows.
  • Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.
  • Shock and anaphylaxis may occur, so carefully monitor the product. If decreased blood pressure, hives, difficulty breathing, etc. occur, immediately discontinue use and take appropriate measures. ”
  • (Explanation) *1 Chlorhexidine at a concentration of 0.5% or higher is highly toxic to the eyes, and if high concentrations of chlorhexidine enter the eye, serious corneal damage will occur15). *2 When diluted with purified water or tap water, chlorhexidine gluconate, which has mild potency, may be contaminated with bacteria such as Pseudomonas spp. and Serratia marcescens. Therefore, it should be sterilized after preparation16).
  • Refer to "VIII. Items related to safety (precautions, etc.)", "2. Contraindications and their reasons (including contraindications in principle)", "6. Important basic precautions, their reasons and treatment methods", "8. Side effects", "14. Precautions for application".
  • VIII. Items related to safety (precautions, etc.)

Additional relevant detail includes (1) Administration route: Do not use for any purpose other than hand disinfection. Answer

The retrieved stability-related material for chlorhexidine gluconate mainly addresses storage conditions, shelf-life, and condition-dependent change(s): (1) Appearance/Properties Chlorhexidine gluconate solution is a colorless to slightly yellow, clear liquid with no odor and a bitter taste. (2) Soluble chlorhexidine gluconate solution is miscible with water or acetic acid (100). Additional stability detail includes 2. Stability of active ingredients under various conditions. Further storage or handling information is supported by Gradually colored by light.. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • (1) Appearance/Properties Chlorhexidine gluconate solution is a colorless to slightly yellow, clear liquid with no odor and a bitter taste. (2) Soluble chlorhexidine gluconate solution is miscible with water or acetic acid (100).
  • 2. Stability of active ingredients under various conditions
  • Gradually colored by light.
  • Expiration date: 3 years after manufacture (based on stability test results) (See section 5. Stability of formulations under various conditions in ``IV. Items related to formulations.'')
  • 3.Storage method/storage conditions
  • Seal tightly and store at room temperature, protected from light.

106. Clinical question

Clinical English: Summarize the clinically relevant warnings, contraindications, and high-priority use restrictions for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: What are the key warnings and contraindications for chlorhexidine gluconate?

Question family: warnings_contra

Answer

Across the retrieved PMDA sources for chlorhexidine gluconate, the most consistent high-priority restrictions involve the following points: (e-IF) became the principle. In line with this change, if there is a revision to the package insert such as ``addition of indications'' or ``revised warnings, contraindications, and important basic precautions'', the latest version of Stericlone® R liquid with added rationale for the revision. Additional clinically relevant restriction(s) include "In order to predict reactions such as shock and anaphylaxis, be sure to thoroughly inquire about your history of hypersensitivity to chlorhexidine preparations and whether you have a predisposition to drug sensitivity before use.". Further caution is supported by [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows.. Evidence was retrieved from 6 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • (e-IF) became the principle. In line with this change, if there is a revision to the package insert such as ``addition of indications'' or ``revised warnings, contraindications, and important basic precautions'', the latest version of Stericlone® R liquid with added rationale for the revision.
  • "In order to predict reactions such as shock and anaphylaxis, be sure to thoroughly inquire about your history of hypersensitivity to chlorhexidine preparations and whether you have a predisposition to drug sensitivity before use."
  • [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows.
  • Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.
  • (Explanation) *1 Chlorhexidine at a concentration of 0.5% or higher is highly toxic to the eyes, and if high concentrations of chlorhexidine enter the eye, serious corneal damage will occur15). *2 When diluted with purified water or tap water, chlorhexidine gluconate, which has mild potency, may be contaminated with bacteria such as Pseudomonas spp. and Serratia marcescens. Therefore, it should be sterilized after preparation16).
  • (1) Administration route: Do not use for any purpose other than hand disinfection. (2) When using: Be careful as there are reports that chemical skin burns may occur if the solution is in contact with the skin for a long period of time.

Question family: pk

Answer

The retrieved pharmacokinetic evidence for chlorhexidine gluconate highlights the following key PK findings: (1) Analysis method not applicable (2) Absorption rate constant not applicable (3) Disappearance rate constant not applicable (4) Clearance not applicable (5) Volume of distribution not applicable (6) Other applicable data not available Additional PK information includes Not applicable (Reference 1: Human [absorption/excretion 15)]). Special-population or disposition-related detail is also mentioned in (Reference 2: Pharmacokinetics in animals [Absorption/Excretion 16)] Even if chlorhexidine gluconate is orally administered to animals, it is hardly absorbed from the digestive tract and is excreted in the feces.. Evidence was retrieved from 5 source PDF file(s).

  • (Reference 2: Pharmacokinetics in animals [Absorption/Excretion 16)] Even if chlorhexidine gluconate is orally administered to animals, it is hardly absorbed from the digestive tract and is excreted in the feces.

111. Clinical question

Clinical English: Compare the warnings for alprazolam and abaloparatide. for chlorhexidine gluconate.

Original question: Compare the warnings for alprazolam and abaloparatide.

Question family: warning

Answer

The retrieved PMDA evidence for chlorhexidine gluconate indicates the following key points: [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows. Additional relevant detail includes Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.. Evidence was retrieved from 5 source PDF file(s).

Key supporting findings

  • [Measures] The precautions for use will be revised as follows.
  • Please refer to the description regarding shock in the [Important Basic Precautions] section.
  • Shock and anaphylaxis may occur, so carefully monitor the product. If decreased blood pressure, hives, difficulty breathing, etc. occur, immediately discontinue use and take appropriate measures. ”
  • (Explanation) *1 Chlorhexidine at a concentration of 0.5% or higher is highly toxic to the eyes, and if high concentrations of chlorhexidine enter the eye, serious corneal damage will occur15). *2 When diluted with purified water or tap water, chlorhexidine gluconate, which has mild potency, may be contaminated with bacteria such as Pseudomonas spp. and Serratia marcescens. Therefore, it should be sterilized after preparation16).
